The Number of Gardens in Paradise
Sanusi enumerates the majority and alternative views on the number of gardens.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the majority view that there are four gardens in Paradise and the alternative view of one garden with many names, supported by Quranic verses.

Core Idea
Paradise's many names highlight its immense blessings, not separate gardens.

Sanusi begins by presenting different scholarly opinions on the number of gardens in Paradise. The majority view, based on Quranic verses, holds that there are four distinct gardens, while others argue that it is a single garden with multiple names reflecting its attributes. Let's examine the evidence and reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic evidence
Read the verses cited (Ar-Rahman 46 and 62) and how they support the four-garden view.
The verses are from Surah Ar-Rahman.
2
Understand the majority view
The author mentions that a group preferred four gardens, and that this is the position of the majority of scholars.
3
Consider the alternative view
Some scholars say it is one garden with names indicating attributes like eternity, delight, etc.
This view unifies the gardens conceptually.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو أربع؟ ورجّحه جماعة لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلِمَنْ خَافَ مَقَامَ رَبِّهِ جَنَّتَانِ) [الرحمن : ٤٦]؛ جنة النعيم وجنة المأوى، ثم قال: ﴿وَمِن دُونِهِمَا جَنَّتَانِ) [الرحمن: ٦٢] أي: جنة عدن وجنة الفردوس، كما قاله بعض المفسرين وهذا ما ذهب إليه الجمهور. أو جنةٌ واحدةٌ وهذه الأسماء كلها جارية عليها لتحقق معانيها فيها، إذ يصدق على الجميع جنةُ عَدْنٍ؛ أي: إقامة وجنة المأوى؛ أي: مأوى المؤمنين، وجنة الخلد ودار السلام؛ لأن جميعها للخلود والسلامة من كل خوف وحُزْنٍ، وجنة النعيم؛ لأنها كلها مشحونة بأصنافه . قوله : (فَلا تَمِلْ لِجَاحِدٍ) أي : فلا تُصْغ لقول منكر لهما بالمرة لكفره كالفلاسفة، أو منكر لوجودهما فيما مضى لبدعته كأبي هاشم وعبد الجبار المعتزليين. وقوله : (ذِي جِنَّهُ) أي : صاحب جنون؛ لأن إنكارهما لا يكاد يصدر عن ذي عقل ؛ فإنه يُؤدي إلى إحالة ما علم من الدين بالضرورة.
Or four? And a group preferred it due to His statement the Most High: 'And for whoever fears the standing of his Lord are two gardens' [Ar-Rahman: 46]; the Garden of Delight and the Garden of Refuge. Then He said: 'And besides these two are two gardens' [Ar-Rahman: 62] meaning the Garden of Eden and the Garden of Firdaws, as some exegetes said. And this is what the majority held. Or it is one garden and all these names apply to it because their meanings are realized in it, for every one is called Garden of Eden, i.e., permanent residence, and Garden of Refuge, i.e., refuge of the believers, and Garden of Eternity and Abode of Peace, because all are for eternity and safety from every fear and grief, and Garden of Delight, because all are filled with its varieties. His statement: 'So do not incline to a denier' means: do not listen to the statement of one who denies them altogether due to his disbelief, like the philosophers, or one who denies their existence in the past due to his innovation, like Abu Hashim and 'Abd al-Jabbar the Mu'tazilites. And His statement: 'possessor of madness' means: possessor of insanity, because their denial is hardly emitted from one of intellect, for it leads to rendering impossible what is known from religion by necessity.
Source pages p. 372

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of a line from the poem, discussing the number of gardens in Paradise and the ruling on those who deny them. First, the author mentions the view that there are four gardens, citing the verse 'for whoever fears the standing of his Lord are two gardens' and then 'and besides these two are two gardens', interpreting them as four distinct gardens. This is the majority view. Alternatively, some say there is only one garden with multiple names, each name reflecting a different attribute: 'Garden of Eden' means permanent residence, 'Garden of Refuge' is refuge for believers, 'Garden of Eternity' and 'Abode of Peace' indicate safety, 'Garden of Delight' indicates being filled with blessings. The author then warns against inclining to a denier (jahid), explaining that 'la tamill' means do not listen to or accept the word of someone who denies these gardens entirely, like the philosophers, or denies their existence in the past, like the Mu'tazilites Abu Hashim and 'Abd al-Jabbar. Such denial is described as madness (dhi jinnah), because it contradicts what is known necessarily from religion, i.e., the existence of Paradise and Hell is a matter of certainty from the Quran and consensus.

Key Terms
جنة (garden)
خلود (eternity)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the gardens are exactly two or four with no flexibility.
Correction: The author presents both views as valid, showing there is room for interpretation.

Checkpoint
According to the majority view, how many gardens are there in Paradise?
A) One
B) Two
C) Four
D) Seven

Key Takeaway
The majority of scholars hold that there are four gardens in Paradise, while others consider it one garden with multiple names indicating its blessings.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The source says Paradise is called 'Abode of Peace' because it is safe from 'every fear and grief.' What specific fear or grief in your life right now are you holding onto that contradicts this promise? Will you let it go today and trust in that peace?
?
If Paradise is one garden with many names, each describing a different blessing (delight, refuge, eternity, peace), which of these aspects do you personally long for most—honestly, in your current state? How does that longing shape your daily choices?
?
The majority opinion holds that there are four distinct gardens. If you truly believed that Paradise has layers and levels, would you be content with the lowest, or would you strive for the highest? What are you doing today to increase your longing for the highest abode?

Refuting the Deniers of Paradise's Gardens
Sanusi warns against deniers of the gardens and categorizes them.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why denying the gardens of Paradise is considered disbelief or innovation, and why it is described as madness.

Core Idea
Denying clear religious truths is a sign of intellectual corruption and spiritual sickness.

After discussing the gardens, Sanusi warns against inclining to those who deny their existence. He identifies two categories of deniers: outright disbelievers like philosophers, and misguided innovators like certain Mu'tazilites. The severity of this denial is such that it is equated with madness. Let's explore why.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of deniers
Philosophers deny the gardens entirely out of disbelief; some Mu'tazilites deny their past existence due to innovation. Note the names: Abu Hashim and 'Abd al-Jabbar.
2
Understand the warning 'la tamill'
The phrase means do not listen or incline to their views. It is a strong prohibition.
3
Grasp why it is called madness
Such denial contradicts what is known necessarily from religion (ma 'ulima min al-din bil-darura), so it is irrational.
This is a very severe condemnation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Or four? And a group preferred it due to His statement the Most High: 'And for whoever fears the standing of his Lord are two gardens' [Ar-Rahman: 46]; the Garden of Delight and the Garden of Refuge. His statement: 'So do not incline to a denier' means: do not listen to the statement of one who denies them altogether due to his disbelief, like the philosophers, or one who denies their existence in the past due to his innovation, like Abu Hashim and 'Abd al-Jabbar the Mu'tazilites. And His statement: 'possessor of madness' means: possessor of insanity, because their denial is hardly emitted from one of intellect, for it leads to rendering impossible what is known from religion by necessity.

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of a line from the poem, discussing the number of gardens in Paradise and the ruling on those who deny them. Key Terms

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that denying Paradise is just a minor theological error.
Correction: The author equates such denial with madness and disbelief, showing its severe gravity.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why is denying the gardens described as madness?
A) Because it is a sign of mental illness
B) Because it contradicts what is known necessarily from religion
C) Because the deniers are philosophers
D) Because the gardens are indescribable

Key Takeaway
Denying the gardens of Paradise is either disbelief (if total denial) or innovation (if denying past existence), and it is considered a form of madness because it contradicts necessary religious knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever found yourself entertaining doubts about the reality of Paradise or Hell? What does this lesson reveal about the spiritual danger of such thoughts? Will you actively seek to strengthen your conviction in these unseen matters?
?
The passage warns not to 'incline' to a denier. In your daily life, what influences—books, people, media—might be subtly inclining you toward doubt or denial? What concrete step will you take today to guard your heart from such influences?
?
If denying Paradise is considered a form of 'madness' because it contradicts clear religious knowledge, how seriously do you take the beliefs that you claim to hold? Does your life reflect a genuine, lived certainty in Paradise, or have you allowed indifference to creep in? What will you change starting now?

The Eternity of Paradise and Hell – Refuting the Jahmiyyah
Definition of 'dara' and refutation of Jahmiyyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of 'دارا خلود' and why the Jahmiyyah view that Paradise and Hell will perish is a rejection of clear Quranic and Sunnah texts.

Core Idea
The eternity of Paradise and Hell is a foundational belief; denial leads to disbelief.

The author begins by clarifying the phrase 'دارا خلود' (two abodes of eternity) from the poem. This phrase is not merely descriptive but serves as a direct refutation of a deviant sect, the Jahmiyyah, who claimed that both Paradise and Hell would eventually end. In this lesson, we explore the meaning of this phrase and why the Jahmiyyah stance is considered kufr.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and its translation
Read the passage carefully to understand the direct meaning.
Notice the author uses a simple definition.
2
Understand 'دار خلود'
The author explains it as a permanent abode of residence. Note the emphasis on permanence.
3
Identify the refutation of Jahmiyyah
The author explicitly refutes the Jahmiyyah who say the abodes perish. Recognize why this is considered disbelief.
The refutation is based on Quran and Sunnah.
4
Reflect on the gravity of this belief
Contemplate why denial of eternal abodes is so serious that it leads to takfir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (دَارًا) خُلُودٍ) أي: دارا إقامةٍ مُؤيَّدةٍ، ورد المصنّف بذلك على الجهمية؛ وهم منسوبون لَجَهم، اسم رجل يقولون بفنائهما وفناء أهلهما، وهم كفار لمخالفتهم للكتاب والسنة. وقوله : (للسَّعِيدِ وَالشَّقِيْ) أي : فالجنةُ دارُ خلودٍ للسعيد، وهو من مات على الإسلام، وإن تقدَّم منه كُفْرٌ، ودخل في السعيد عصاة المؤمنين، فدار خلودهم الجنة، فلا يخلدون في النار إن دخلوها، بل لا يدوم عذابهم فيها مُدَّة بقائهم؛ لأنهم يموتون بعد الدخول بلحظة ما يعلم إلا الله ،مقدارها، فلا يحيون حتى يخرجوا منها. والمراد بموتهم أنهم يفقدون إحساس ألم العذاب، لا أنهم يموتون موتاً حقيقياً بخروج الروح، وبعضهم اختار أنهم يموتون حقيقة. والنار دار خلود للشقي: وهو من مات على الكفر، وإن عاش طول عمره على الإيمان، ودخل في الشقي : الكافر الجاهل، والمعاند ومن بالغ في النظر فلم يصل إلى الحق، وترك التقليد الواجب عليه ولا يدخل فيه أطفال المشركين، بل هم في الجنة على الصحيح من أقوال كثيرة، فمنها أنهم في النار ، وقيل : على الأعراف، إلى غير ذلك من الأقوال. وأما أطفالُ المؤمنين ففي الجنة عند الجمهور، ومقابله أنهم في المشيئة، وأنكر ذلك القول، وهذا في غير أولاد الأنبياء، وأما أولاد الأنبياء ففى الجنة إجماعاً . ولا فرق في السعيد والشقي بين الإنس والجن، ويدل على ما ذكر من أن الجنة دار خلود للسعيد والنار دار خلود للشقي قوله تعالى: ﴿فَمِنْهُمْ شَفِي وَسَعِيدٌ ... [هود : ١٠٥] الآية، والمراد بالسموات والأرض في هذه الآية سقف النار وأرضُها، وسقف الجنة ،وأرضُها، لا سماء الدنيا وأرضُها لتبدلهما.
His statement: 'two abodes of eternity' means two abodes of permanent residence, and the author refuted thereby the Jahmiyyah; they are attributed to Jahm, a man who says they (Paradise and Hell) will perish and their inhabitants will perish, and they are disbelievers due to their opposition to the Book and the Sunnah. And His statement: 'for the blessed and the wretched' means: Paradise is an abode of eternity for the blessed, and he is the one who died upon Islam, even if disbelief preceded him, and the sinful believers are included in the blessed, so their abode of eternity is Paradise, so they will not remain eternally in the Fire if they enter it, but their punishment will not last during their period of stay, because they die after entering by a moment whose measure none knows but Allah, so they do not live until they come out of it. And what is meant by their death is that they lose the sensation of the pain of punishment, not that they die a real death by the departure of the soul, and some chose that they die in reality. And the Fire is an abode of eternity for the wretched: he is the one who died upon disbelief, even if he lived his entire life upon faith, and included in the wretched is the ignorant disbeliever, and the obstinate one, and the one who exerted effort in reflection but did not reach the truth, and abandoned the obligatory imitation (taqlid). And it does not include the children of polytheists; rather they are in Paradise according to the correct among many statements: among them that they are in the Fire, and it is said upon the Heights (al-A'raf), and other statements. As for the children of believers, they are in Paradise according to the majority, and its opposite is that they are under the will (mashi'ah), and that statement is rejected. And this is other than the children of prophets, for the children of prophets are in Paradise by consensus. And there is no difference between humans and jinn regarding the blessed and the wretched. And what indicates what has been mentioned, that Paradise is an abode of eternity for the blessed and the Fire is an abode of eternity for the wretched, is His statement the Most High: 'And among them are wretched and blessed...' [Hud: 105] the verse, and what is meant by the heavens and the earth in this verse is the ceiling of the Fire and its ground, and the ceiling of Paradise and its ground, not the heaven of this world and its earth, because they change.
Source pages p. 372

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the line 'دارا خلود' (two abodes of eternity) from the poem. The author begins by clarifying that 'darani' means two permanent abodes, and the poet (al-Laqqani) refutes the Jahmiyyah with this statement, who are followers of Jahm ibn Safwan. The Jahmiyyah claim that Paradise and Hell will eventually perish along with their inhabitants; this view is deemed disbelief because it contradicts the Quran and Sunnah. Next, the author explains 'lil sa'idi wa al-shaqi' (for the blessed and the wretched). The blessed (sa'id) is the one who dies upon Islam, even if he had committed disbelief before. This includes sinful believers ('usat al-mu'minin) — they are ultimately destined for Paradise, even if they enter Hell temporarily due to their sins. Their punishment in Hell will not be eternal; rather, they will die (feel no sensation) after a short period known only to Allah, then be brought out. This death is interpreted as the loss of pain sensation, not literal death, though some scholars say it is literal. Then the author defines the wretched (shaqi) as the one who dies upon disbelief, even if he lived a long life of faith. This includes the ignorant disbeliever, the obstinate, and the one who, despite theoretical reflection, failed to reach the truth and abandoned the required taqlid (imitation of true belief). The author further addresses the fate of children. Children of polytheists are not included in the wretched; the correct view is that they are in Paradise, though there are other opinions (Fire, al-A'raf, etc.). Children of believers are in Paradise according to the majority, with an opposing view that they are under Allah's will (mashi'ah), but the author rejects that other statement. Children of prophets are definitely in Paradise by consensus. Finally, the author states that the rulings of blessed and wretched apply equally to humans and jinn, and supports the entire explanation with the verse 'And among them are wretched and blessed' (Hud: 105), interpreting the 'heavens and earth' in that verse as the ceiling and ground of the Fire and Paradise, not the worldly heaven and earth, because the latter undergo change.

Key Terms
دار خلود (abode of eternity)
جهمية (Jahmiyyah)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Paradise and Hell will eventually perish with their inhabitants.
Correction: The Quran and Sunnah clearly state they are eternal; belief otherwise is kufr.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why are the Jahmiyyah considered disbelievers?
A) Because they believe in the eternity of Paradise and Hell
B) Because they deny the creation of Paradise and Hell
C) Because they claim Paradise and Hell will perish
D) Because they reject the prophets

Key Takeaway
The eternity of Paradise and Hell is an established truth; opposing it is a rejection of Islam.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly live each day with the certainty that your deeds are being weighed for an eternal destination that will never end? Or do you act as if this life is all that matters, ignoring the permanence of what awaits?
?
If you were to meet someone who denies the eternity of Paradise and Hell, would you have the courage to warn them, or would you remain silent for fear of being called extreme? Your silence might enable their disbelief.
?
The Jahmiyyah were declared disbelievers for rejecting this truth. Is there any belief in your heart that contradicts the clear texts of the Quran and Sunnah? What are you doing to uproot it?

Defining the Blessed (Sa'id) and the Wretched (Shaqi)
Definitions of sa'id and shaqi with details on sinful believers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definitions of 'sa'id' (blessed) and 'shaqi' (wretched) as used in Islamic theology, and the special ruling for sinful believers.

Core Idea
Your final state depends on the condition upon death, not your entire life.

After establishing the eternity of the two abodes, the author now specifies who qualifies as blessed (sa'id) and who as wretched (shaqi). This is a crucial clarification because it refutes both extreme optimism (all Muslims go to Heaven regardless) and excessive despair (sins doom a believer forever). In this lesson, we unpack these definitions and see how the author handles the complex case of sinful believers.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on sa'id and shaqi
Read from 'وقوله : (للسَّعِيدِ وَالشَّقِيْ)' to 'ولا يدخل فيه أطفال المشركين'.
2
Analyse the definition of sa'id
Note that sa'id is one who dies upon Islam, even if he had previous disbelief, and includes sinful believers.
3
Understand the fate of sinful believers
They will not remain in Hell forever; they die after a short punishment and then enter Paradise.
The death is interpreted as loss of sensation.
4
Analyse the definition of shaqi
Shaqi is one who dies upon kufr, including the ignorant, obstinate, and those who failed in theoretical reflection.
5
Notice the exclusion of polytheist children
The passage explicitly excludes children of polytheists from being considered shaqi.
This is a transition to the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (دَارًا) خُلُودٍ) أي: دارا إقامةٍ مُؤيَّدةٍ، ورد المصنّف بذلك على الجهمية؛ وهم منسوبون لَجَهم، اسم رجل يقولون بفنائهما وفناء أهلهما، وهم كفار لمخالفتهم للكتاب والسنة. وقوله : (للسَّعِيدِ وَالشَّقِيْ) أي : فالجنةُ دارُ خلودٍ للسعيد، وهو من مات على الإسلام، وإن تقدَّم منه كُفْرٌ، ودخل في السعيد عصاة المؤمنين، فدار خلودهم الجنة، فلا يخلدون في النار إن دخلوها، بل لا يدوم عذابهم فيها مُدَّة بقائهم؛ لأنهم يموتون بعد الدخول بلحظة ما يعلم إلا الله ،مقدارها، فلا يحيون حتى يخرجوا منها. والمراد بموتهم أنهم يفقدون إحساس ألم العذاب، لا أنهم يموتون موتاً حقيقياً بخروج الروح، وبعضهم اختار أنهم يموتون حقيقة. والنار دار خلود للشقي: وهو من مات على الكفر، وإن عاش طول عمره على الإيمان، ودخل في الشقي : الكافر الجاهل، والمعاند ومن بالغ في النظر فلم يصل إلى الحق، وترك التقليد الواجب عليه ولا يدخل فيه أطفال المشركين، بل هم في الجنة على الصحيح من أقوال كثيرة، فمنها أنهم في النار ، وقيل : على الأعراف، إلى غير ذلك من الأقوال. وأما أطفالُ المؤمنين ففي الجنة عند الجمهور، ومقابله أنهم في المشيئة، وأنكر ذلك القول، وهذا في غير أولاد الأنبياء، وأما أولاد الأنبياء ففى الجنة إجماعاً . ولا فرق في السعيد والشقي بين الإنس والجن، ويدل على ما ذكر من أن الجنة دار خلود للسعيد والنار دار خلود للشقي قوله تعالى: ﴿فَمِنْهُمْ شَفِي وَسَعِيدٌ ... [هود : ١٠٥] الآية، والمراد بالسموات والأرض في هذه الآية سقف النار وأرضُها، وسقف الجنة ،وأرضُها، لا سماء الدنيا وأرضُها لتبدلهما.
His statement: 'two abodes of eternity' means two abodes of permanent residence, and the author refuted thereby the Jahmiyyah; they are attributed to Jahm, a man who says they (Paradise and Hell) will perish and their inhabitants will perish, and they are disbelievers due to their opposition to the Book and the Sunnah. And His statement: 'for the blessed and the wretched' means: Paradise is an abode of eternity for the blessed, and he is the one who died upon Islam, even if disbelief preceded him, and the sinful believers are included in the blessed, so their abode of eternity is Paradise, so they will not remain eternally in the Fire if they enter it, but their punishment will not last during their period of stay, because they die after entering by a moment whose measure none knows but Allah, so they do not live until they come out of it. And what is meant by their death is that they lose the sensation of the pain of punishment, not that they die a real death by the departure of the soul, and some chose that they die in reality. And the Fire is an abode of eternity for the wretched: he is the one who died upon disbelief, even if he lived his entire life upon faith, and included in the wretched is the ignorant disbeliever, and the obstinate one, and the one who exerted effort in reflection but did not reach the truth, and abandoned the obligatory imitation (taqlid). And it does not include the children of polytheists; rather they are in Paradise according to the correct among many statements: among them that they are in the Fire, and it is said upon the Heights (al-A'raf), and other statements. As for the children of believers, they are in Paradise according to the majority, and its opposite is that they are under the will (mashi'ah), and that statement is rejected. And this is other than the children of prophets, for the children of prophets are in Paradise by consensus. And there is no difference between humans and jinn regarding the blessed and the wretched. And what indicates what has been mentioned, that Paradise is an abode of eternity for the blessed and the Fire is an abode of eternity for the wretched, is His statement the Most High: 'And among them are wretched and blessed...' [Hud: 105] the verse, and what is meant by the heavens and the earth in this verse is the ceiling of the Fire and its ground, and the ceiling of Paradise and its ground, not the heaven of this world and its earth, because they change.
Source pages p. 372

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the line 'دارا خلود' (two abodes of eternity) from the poem. The author begins by clarifying that 'darani' means two permanent abodes, and the poet (al-Laqqani) refutes the Jahmiyyah with this statement, who are followers of Jahm ibn Safwan. The Jahmiyyah claim that Paradise and Hell will eventually perish along with their inhabitants; this view is deemed disbelief because it contradicts the Quran and Sunnah. Next, the author explains 'lil sa'idi wa al-shaqi' (for the blessed and the wretched). The blessed (sa'id) is the one who dies upon Islam, even if he had committed disbelief before. This includes sinful believers ('usat al-mu'minin) — they are ultimately destined for Paradise, even if they enter Hell temporarily due to their sins. Their punishment in Hell will not be eternal; rather, they will die (feel no sensation) after a short period known only to Allah, then be brought out. This death is interpreted as the loss of pain sensation, not literal death, though some scholars say it is literal. Then the author defines the wretched (shaqi) as the one who dies upon disbelief, even if he lived a long life of faith. This includes the ignorant disbeliever, the obstinate, and the one who, despite theoretical reflection, failed to reach the truth and abandoned the required taqlid (imitation of true belief). The author further addresses the fate of children. Children of polytheists are not included in the wretched; the correct view is that they are in Paradise, though there are other opinions (Fire, al-A'raf, etc.). Children of believers are in Paradise according to the majority, with an opposing view that they are under Allah's will (mashi'ah), but the author rejects that other statement. Children of prophets are definitely in Paradise by consensus. Finally, the author states that the rulings of blessed and wretched apply equally to humans and jinn, and supports the entire explanation with the verse 'And among them are wretched and blessed' (Hud: 105), interpreting the 'heavens and earth' in that verse as the ceiling and ground of the Fire and Paradise, not the worldly heaven and earth, because the latter undergo change.

Key Terms
سعيد (blessed)
شقي (wretched)
عصاة المؤمنين (sinful believers)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Sinful Muslims will burn in Hell forever.
Correction: They may enter Hell temporarily but will eventually be brought to Paradise; they do not remain eternally.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens to sinful believers who enter Hell?
A) They remain in Hell forever
B) They die after a short period and then are taken out to Paradise
C) They never enter Hell
D) They are annihilated

Key Takeaway
One's final state upon death determines blessedness or wretchedness, not the entirety of one's life.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to die right now, would you be classified as sa'id or shaqi? What evidence from your life supports that?
?
Think of a sin you commit repeatedly. Does the promise that sinful believers are ultimately saved give you comfort or concern? Why?
?
How does knowing that the final state at death determines everything change how you view your own daily choices and repentance?

The Fate of Children and Jinn in the Afterlife
Rulings on children of various groups and jinn, with Quranic proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the correct Islamic position on the fate of children of polytheists, believers, and prophets, as well as the parallel ruling for jinn.

Core Idea
Children of disbelievers are in Paradise, children of believers are in Paradise, and children of prophets are definitely in Paradise.

The author has defined the blessed and wretched and excluded children of polytheists from the wretched. He now elaborates on the fate of various categories of children, addressing a well-known theological dispute. This lesson clarifies the correct view according to the author (and the majority) and also confirms that the same rulings apply to jinn.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on children and jinn
Read from 'بل هم في الجنة على الصحيح' to the end.
2
Identify the correct view on polytheist children
The author states they are in Paradise, though he lists other opinions.
3
Understand the ruling for children of believers and prophets
Majority holds believers' children are in Paradise; consensus on prophets' children.
4
Recognize the applicability to jinn
The same categories of blessed and wretched apply to jinn as to humans.
5
Analyse the Qur'anic evidence
The verse from Hud supports the eternity of abodes, with a specific interpretation of 'heavens and earth'.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson teaches that every child, regardless of their parents' religion, is destined for Paradise. Does your heart truly accept that Allah's mercy encompasses even the children of those who oppose Him? When you see a non-Muslim family, do you silently judge their children's fate based on your own understanding, or do you entrust them to Allah's promise? What concrete step can you take today to remove any trace of spiritual arrogance from your heart regarding this issue?
?
The author extends the ruling to jinn, reminding you that Allah's justice and mercy apply to all conscious beings. Have you ever considered your own accountability in light of the fact that even unseen creatures are judged by the same standard? If you were to face Allah tonight, would you be among the 'sa'eed' (blessed) or 'shaqiy' (wretched)? What change in your daily habits would reflect the urgency of that question?
?
Knowing that children of prophets are in Paradise by consensus, do you truly live as if you are a follower of the Prophet Muhammad? If you were to die tomorrow, would your faith be strong enough to hope for the same mercy for your own children? How can you better prepare your family to be among the blessed, without assuming that lineage alone guarantees anything?

The Death of the Wicked: Loss of Sensation, Not True Death
The commentator defines death of the wicked as loss of pain sensation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand what is meant by the death of the people of Hell according to the commentator, including the difference between true death and loss of sensation.

Core Idea
The wicked do not truly die; they only lose sensation of pain.

This lesson introduces a key concept in eschatology: the nature of the punishment of the wicked. The commentator clarifies that their 'death' is not the departure of the soul but the loss of pain sensation, with a minority view holding true death.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage on death
Read the Arabic sentence defining the death of the wicked. Focus on the key phrase 'يفقدون إحساس ألم العذاب'.
Notice the contrast between 'موت حقيقي' and loss of sensation.
2
Identify the two opinions
The passage presents two views: the author's view (loss of sensation) and a minority view (true death). Identify each.
3
Understand the theological significance
Why does the commentator emphasize loss of sensation? This underscores that punishment is perpetual; the wicked remain alive to suffer.
This connects to the concept of eternity in Hell.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السمعيات
والمراد بموتهم أنهم يفقدون إحساس ألم العذاب، لا أنهم يموتون موتاً حقيقياً بخروج الروح، وبعضهم اختار أنهم يموتون حقيقة.
والنار دار خلود للشقي: وهو من مات على الكفر، وإن عاش طول عمره على الإيمان، ودخل في الشقي : الكافر الجاهل، والمعاند ومن بالغ في النظر فلم يصل إلى الحق، وترك التقليد الواجب عليه ولا يدخل فيه أطفال المشركين، بل هم في الجنة على الصحيح من أقوال كثيرة، فمنها أنهم في النار ، وقيل : على الأعراف، إلى غير ذلك من الأقوال.
وأما أطفالُ المؤمنين ففي الجنة عند الجمهور، ومقابله أنهم في المشيئة، وأنكر ذلك القول، وهذا في غير أولاد الأنبياء، وأما أولاد الأنبياء ففى الجنة إجماعاً . ولا فرق في السعيد والشقي بين الإنس والجن. خلاف الجن مشهور على القول بعدم تكليفهم قبل سيد الوجود، وعلى القول بالتكليف فالنعيم عند الحنفية فيه ثلاثة أقوال، والجمهور وفيهم صاحبا أبي حنيفة أن طائعهم منعم بالجنة، وقد نقل ابن حزم القول بعدم تكليفهم قبل نبينا عليه الصلاة والسلام وقال : كانوا متطوعين بالإيمان في شريعة موسى عليه السلام قال السبكي : ( ولا شك أنهم مكلفون في الأمم الماضية كهذه الأمة، إما بسماعهم من الرسول، أو من صادق عنه، وكونه إنسيًا أو جنيًّا لا قاطع به، وظاهر القرآن يشهد للضحاك، والأكثرون على خلافه). ويدل على ما ذكر من أن الجنة دار خلود للسعيد والنار دار خلود للشقي قوله تعالى: ﴿فَمِنْهُمْ شَفِي وَسَعِيدٌ ... [هود : ١٠٥] الآية، والمراد بالسموات والأرض في هذه الآية سقف النار وأرضُها، وسقف الجنة ،وأرضُها، لا سماء الدنيا وأرضُها لتبدلهما
And the intended meaning of their death is that they lose sensation of the pain of punishment, not that they die a true death by the departure of the soul, and some chose that they truly die. And the Fire is an abode of eternity for the wretched: he who dies upon disbelief, even if he lived his entire life upon faith. And included in the wretched are: the ignorant disbeliever, the obstinate one, and one who exerted in inquiry but did not reach the truth, and abandoned the obligatory imitation. And the children of the polytheists are not included in it; rather they are in Paradise according to the correct view among many opinions, among them that they are in the Fire, and it was said: on the Heights, and other such opinions. And as for the children of the believers, they are in Paradise according to the majority, and the opposite is that they are in the divine will, and that saying is denied. And this is regarding other than the children of the prophets; as for the children of the prophets, they are in Paradise by consensus. And there is no difference between humans and jinn regarding the blessed and the wretched. The disagreement about jinn is well-known: according to the opinion that they are not obligated before the Master of existence, and according to the opinion of obligation, then the bliss with the Hanafis has three sayings, and the majority including the two companions of Abu Hanifa hold that the obedient among them is blessed in Paradise. And Ibn Hazm narrated the opinion that they are not obligated before our Prophet, peace be upon him, and he said: they were voluntary believers in the law of Moses, peace be upon him. Al-Subki said: 'And there is no doubt that they are obligated in past nations like this nation, either by hearing from the messenger or from a truthful source about him, and that the being human or jinn is not definitive, and the apparent Quran bears witness to al-Dahhak, and the majority are contrary to him.' And it indicates what was mentioned, that Paradise is an abode of eternity for the blessed and the Fire is an abode of eternity for the wretched, the saying of the Most High: 'Then among them are wretched and blessed...' [Hud 11:105] the verse. And the intended meaning of the heavens and the earth in this verse is the ceiling of the Fire and its earth, and the ceiling of Paradise and its earth, not the heaven of the world and its earth, because they will be replaced.
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This passage is a combined definition, classification, and proof. It first defines what is meant by the death of the people of hell: they do not die a true death by soul departure but rather lose sensation of pain, with a minority opinion that they truly die. Then it classifies the wretched (al-shaqi): those who die upon disbelief, including the ignorant disbeliever, the obstinate one, and one who failed in inquiry while neglecting obligatory imitation. Children of polytheists are excluded from the wretched and are in Paradise according to the correct view. Children of believers are in Paradise by majority opinion, with a contrary view that they are under God's will, but the consensus is that children of prophets are in Paradise. The same categories apply to jinn as to humans, with a lengthy note on the disagreement about jinn's obligation. Finally, the author provides a proof from the Quran (Hud 11:105) that Paradise and Hell are eternal abodes, and he interprets 'heavens and earth' in that verse as the ceilings and floors of Hell and Paradise, not the worldly heavens and earth.

Key Terms
موت حقيقي
شقي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the wicked actually die and cease to exist.
Correction: The passage clarifies they only lose sensation; they remain alive to experience punishment.

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what does the 'death' of the wicked refer to?
A) The departure of the soul
B) Loss of sensation of pain
C) Complete annihilation
D) None of the above

Key Takeaway
The death of the wicked means losing the sensation of pain, not true death.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson says that for the wicked, death only means losing the sensation of pain, not an end to existence. How does this reality make you feel about the accountability awaiting you? What would it mean for you if your own sins, if unrepented, led to such a death?
?
If you could only escape punishment by losing the sensation of pain but still remain in Hell, would that be enough for you? Why or why not, and what does your answer reveal about your current relationship with Allah and your urgency to seek forgiveness?
?
The passage mentions a minority opinion that the wicked truly die. Even if that were true, would you risk being wrong? Today, what concrete step will you take to ensure you are among the saved, not among those who merely lose sensation?

Who Are the Wretched? Excluding Children of Polytheists
The commentator classifies the wretched and determines the fate of polytheist children.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the classification of the wretched (al-shaqi) and the correct opinion that children of polytheists are not among them, but are in Paradise.

Core Idea
Children of polytheists are in Paradise, not Hell.

This lesson defines who is considered wretched (shaqi) in Islamic theology: those who die in disbelief. It then addresses the case of children of polytheists, concluding that they are not wretched and are in Paradise according to the correct view.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of shaqi
Read the Arabic sentence defining the wretched: 'والنار دار خلود للشقي: وهو من مات على الكفر'.
Note the phrase 'وإن عاش طول عمره على الإيمان' which emphasizes that final state matters.
2
Identify the categories included
The passage lists three subcategories of the wretched. Find them: the ignorant disbeliever, the obstinate, and the one who failed in inquiry while neglecting obligatory taqlid.
3
Understand the exception of polytheist children
The passage explicitly excludes children of polytheists from the wretched and states the correct view is Paradise. Note the other opinions mentioned.
This is a significant theological ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السمعيات
والمراد بموتهم أنهم يفقدون إحساس ألم العذاب، لا أنهم يموتون موتاً حقيقياً بخروج الروح، وبعضهم اختار أنهم يموتون حقيقة.
والنار دار خلود للشقي: وهو من مات على الكفر، وإن عاش طول عمره على الإيمان، ودخل في الشقي : الكافر الجاهل، والمعاند ومن بالغ في النظر فلم يصل إلى الحق، وترك التقليد الواجب عليه ولا يدخل فيه أطفال المشركين، بل هم في الجنة على الصحيح من أقوال كثيرة، فمنها أنهم في النار ، وقيل : على الأعراف، إلى غير ذلك من الأقوال.
وأما أطفالُ المؤمنين ففي الجنة عند الجمهور، ومقابله أنهم في المشيئة، وأنكر ذلك القول، وهذا في غير أولاد الأنبياء، وأما أولاد الأنبياء ففى الجنة إجماعاً . ولا فرق في السعيد والشقي بين الإنس والجن. خلاف الجن مشهور على القول بعدم تكليفهم قبل سيد الوجود، وعلى القول بالتكليف فالنعيم عند الحنفية فيه ثلاثة أقوال، والجمهور وفيهم صاحبا أبي حنيفة أن طائعهم منعم بالجنة، وقد نقل ابن حزم القول بعدم تكليفهم قبل نبينا عليه الصلاة والسلام وقال : كانوا متطوعين بالإيمان في شريعة موسى عليه السلام قال السبكي : ( ولا شك أنهم مكلفون في الأمم الماضية كهذه الأمة، إما بسماعهم من الرسول، أو من صادق عنه، وكونه إنسيًا أو جنيًّا لا قاطع به، وظاهر القرآن يشهد للضحاك، والأكثرون على خلافه). ويدل على ما ذكر من أن الجنة دار خلود للسعيد والنار دار خلود للشقي قوله تعالى: ﴿فَمِنْهُمْ شَفِي وَسَعِيدٌ ... [هود : ١٠٥] الآية، والمراد بالسموات والأرض في هذه الآية سقف النار وأرضُها، وسقف الجنة ،وأرضُها، لا سماء الدنيا وأرضُها لتبدلهما
And the intended meaning of their death is that they lose sensation of the pain of punishment, not that they die a true death by the departure of the soul, and some chose that they truly die. And the Fire is an abode of eternity for the wretched: he who dies upon disbelief, even if he lived his entire life upon faith. And included in the wretched are: the ignorant disbeliever, the obstinate one, and one who exerted in inquiry but did not reach the truth, and abandoned the obligatory imitation. And the children of the polytheists are not included in it; rather they are in Paradise according to the correct view among many opinions, among them that they are in the Fire, and it was said: on the Heights, and other such opinions. And as for the children of the believers, they are in Paradise according to the majority, and the opposite is that they are in the divine will, and that saying is denied. And this is regarding other than the children of the prophets; as for the children of the prophets, they are in Paradise by consensus. And there is no difference between humans and jinn regarding the blessed and the wretched. The disagreement about jinn is well-known: according to the opinion that they are not obligated before the Master of existence, and according to the opinion of obligation, then the bliss with the Hanafis has three sayings, and the majority including the two companions of Abu Hanifa hold that the obedient among them is blessed in Paradise. And Ibn Hazm narrated the opinion that they are not obligated before our Prophet, peace be upon him, and he said: they were voluntary believers in the law of Moses, peace be upon him. Al-Subki said: 'And there is no doubt that they are obligated in past nations like this nation, either by hearing from the messenger or from a truthful source about him, and that the being human or jinn is not definitive, and the apparent Quran bears witness to al-Dahhak, and the majority are contrary to him.' And it indicates what was mentioned, that Paradise is an abode of eternity for the blessed and the Fire is an abode of eternity for the wretched, the saying of the Most High: 'Then among them are wretched and blessed...' [Hud 11:105] the verse. And the intended meaning of the heavens and the earth in this verse is the ceiling of the Fire and its earth, and the ceiling of Paradise and its earth, not the heaven of the world and its earth, because they will be replaced.
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This passage is a combined definition, classification, and proof. It first defines what is meant by the death of the people of hell: they do not die a true death by soul departure but rather lose sensation of pain, with a minority opinion that they truly die. Then it classifies the wretched (al-shaqi): those who die upon disbelief, including the ignorant disbeliever, the obstinate one, and one who failed in inquiry while neglecting obligatory imitation. Children of polytheists are excluded from the wretched and are in Paradise according to the correct view. Children of believers are in Paradise by majority opinion, with a contrary view that they are under God's will, but the consensus is that children of prophets are in Paradise. The same categories apply to jinn as to humans, with a lengthy note on the disagreement about jinn's obligation. Finally, the author provides a proof from the Quran (Hud 11:105) that Paradise and Hell are eternal abodes, and he interprets 'heavens and earth' in that verse as the ceilings and floors of Hell and Paradise, not the worldly heavens and earth.

Key Terms
شقي
سعيد
أطفال المشركين
تقليد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think children of polytheists will be in Hell.
Correction: The correct view is that they are in Paradise, as stated by the commentator.

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what is the correct view regarding the children of polytheists?
A) They are in Hell
B) They are in Paradise
C) They are on the Heights
D) They are under God's will

Key Takeaway
The children of polytheists are excluded from the wretched and are in Paradise by the correct opinion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage defines the wretched as one who dies upon disbelief, even if they lived their whole life in faith. Does your daily life reflect a fear of ending in disbelief? What concrete steps do you take to ensure your final moments are upon imān?
?
Children of polytheists are saved by Allah's mercy due to their innocence. If you have children, do you trust in their innate fitrah or do you rely on your own efforts to guide them? And if you are not a parent, what about your own childhood—are you confident that your faith today is your own, not just inherited?
?
The three categories of wretched include those who fail to seek the truth diligently or who obstinately reject it. Honestly examine your heart: have you ever avoided a difficult question about your faith out of laziness or fear? What truth have you been neglecting, and what will you do this week to pursue it?

beginner

Fate of Children of Believers and Prophets
The commentator states the fate of children of believers and prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the different rulings regarding the fate of children: children of believers are in Paradise by majority, while children of prophets are in Paradise by consensus.

Core Idea
Children of believers are in Paradise; children of prophets are in Paradise by unanimous agreement.

This lesson addresses the fate of children who die before puberty. The commentator presents the majority view that children of believers are in Paradise, with a minority view placing them under God's will. For children of prophets, there is consensus that they are in Paradise.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on children of believers and prophets
Read the Arabic section that begins 'وأما أطفالُ المؤمنين' and continues through 'إجماعاً'.
Pay attention to the phrases 'عند الجمهور' and 'إجماعاً'.
2
Identify the majority and minority opinions for believers' children
The majority say Paradise; a minority say under God's will. Note that the author denies the minority view.
3
Understand the consensus on prophets' children
For children of prophets, there is consensus (ijma) that they are in Paradise.
This is a higher level of certainty.

?

?

?
The minority view that children of believers are subject to God's will is denied. Examine your own heart: do you ever doubt that all children of believers are in Paradise? What does that doubt say about your trust in Allah's mercy?

Jinn: Same Fate as Humans, Disagreement on Obligation
The commentator discusses jinn's fate and obligation dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that jinn are subject to the same classification of blessed and wretched as humans, and the disagreement regarding their obligation before Islam.

Core Idea
Jinn share the same fate as humans, but scholars disagree about their obligation before the Prophet.

This lesson extends the discussion to jinn. The commentator states that there is no difference between humans and jinn in terms of being blessed or wretched. He then notes the well-known disagreement about whether jinn were obligated before the arrival of Islam, and cites various opinions including Ibn Hazm and al-Subki.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on jinn
Read from 'ولا فرق في السعيد والشقي بين الإنس والجن' to the end of al-Subki's quote.
Note the key phrase 'ولا فرق'.
2
Understand the equal classification
The passage affirms that jinn and humans are treated equally regarding bliss and wretchedness.
3
Identify the different opinions on obligation
There are opinions that jinn were not obligated before Prophet Muhammad (Ibn Hazm) and that they were obligated (al-Subki and majority). Note the Hanafi positions mentioned.
This is a complex dispute with multiple layers.

Source Text

Commentary

According to the majority of Hanafis and their two companions, what is the fate of obedient jinn?
A) They are not obligated
B) They are in Paradise
C) They are in Hell
D) They are on the Heights

Jinn are subject to the same classification of bliss and wretchedness as humans, with a dispute about their obligation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If jinn are accountable to the same law as humans, yet unseen and living alongside us, what does that imply about your awareness of their presence and your accountability before Allah? How does this change the way you live your daily life? Ask yourself: Are you considering the unseen realities as seriously as the seen?
?
The disagreement about jinn's obligation shows that even scholars differ on details of the unseen. How does that affect your humility when discussing matters of faith? Are you quick to assert certainty where even the scholars hold differing views? Commit to speaking about such matters with humility.
?
The fact that jinn and humans are equal in being blessed or wretched means that your status in the afterlife is not determined by your species but by your obedience. How does that shift your perspective on your own efforts? Are you relying on being human to guarantee salvation, or are you actively working to be among the obedient? Make a concrete plan to increase your obedience today.

Quranic Proof: Paradise and Hell as Eternal Abodes
The commentator provides a Quranic proof for the eternity of Paradise and Hell.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Quranic proof for the eternity of Paradise and Hell from Surah Hud, and the interpretation of the heavens and earth in that verse.

Core Idea
Paradise and Hell are eternal abodes, as proven by the Quran.

This lesson presents the Quranic evidence supporting the eternal nature of Paradise and Hell. The commentator cites verse 11:105, interpreting that the 'heavens and earth' mentioned refer to the ceilings and floors of Hell and Paradise, not the worldly ones.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic verse and its interpretation
Read the Arabic passage that includes the verse and its explanation. Note the verse ending with 'الآية' and the interpretation starting with 'والمراد'.
2
Understand the commentator's exegesis of 'heavens and earth'
The commentator explains that 'heavens and earth' in this context mean the ceilings and floors of Paradise and Hell, not the current heavens and earth, because they will be replaced.
This is an important exegetical point.
3
Realize that the verse proves eternal abodes
The verse indicates that among people are wretched and blessed, implying eternal states. The commentator uses it to support the previous claims.
Connect this to the doctrine of immortality of paradise and hell.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السمعيات
والمراد بموتهم أنهم يفقدون إحساس ألم العذاب، لا أنهم يموتون موتاً حقيقياً بخروج الروح، وبعضهم اختار أنهم يموتون حقيقة.
والنار دار خلود للشقي: وهو من مات على الكفر، وإن عاش طول عمره على الإيمان، ودخل في الشقي : الكافر الجاهل، والمعاند ومن بالغ في النظر فلم يصل إلى الحق، وترك التقليد الواجب عليه ولا يدخل فيه أطفال المشركين، بل هم في الجنة على الصحيح من أقوال كثيرة، فمنها أنهم في النار ، وقيل : على الأعراف، إلى غير ذلك من الأقوال.
وأما أطفالُ المؤمنين ففي الجنة عند الجمهور، ومقابله أنهم في المشيئة، وأنكر ذلك القول، وهذا في غير أولاد الأنبياء، وأما أولاد الأنبياء ففى الجنة إجماعاً . ولا فرق في السعيد والشقي بين الإنس والجن. خلاف الجن مشهور على القول بعدم تكليفهم قبل سيد الوجود، وعلى القول بالتكليف فالنعيم عند الحنفية فيه ثلاثة أقوال، والجمهور وفيهم صاحبا أبي حنيفة أن طائعهم منعم بالجنة، وقد نقل ابن حزم القول بعدم تكليفهم قبل نبينا عليه الصلاة والسلام وقال : كانوا متطوعين بالإيمان في شريعة موسى عليه السلام قال السبكي : ( ولا شك أنهم مكلفون في الأمم الماضية كهذه الأمة، إما بسماعهم من الرسول، أو من صادق عنه، وكونه إنسيًا أو جنيًّا لا قاطع به، وظاهر القرآن يشهد للضحاك، والأكثرون على خلافه). ويدل على ما ذكر من أن الجنة دار خلود للسعيد والنار دار خلود للشقي قوله تعالى: ﴿فَمِنْهُمْ شَفِي وَسَعِيدٌ ... [هود : ١٠٥] الآية، والمراد بالسموات والأرض في هذه الآية سقف النار وأرضُها، وسقف الجنة ،وأرضُها، لا سماء الدنيا وأرضُها لتبدلهما
And the intended meaning of their death is that they lose sensation of the pain of punishment, not that they die a true death by the departure of the soul, and some chose that they truly die. And the Fire is an abode of eternity for the wretched: he who dies upon disbelief, even if he lived his entire life upon faith. And included in the wretched are: the ignorant disbeliever, the obstinate one, and one who exerted in inquiry but did not reach the truth, and abandoned the obligatory imitation. And the children of the polytheists are not included in it; rather they are in Paradise according to the correct view among many opinions, among them that they are in the Fire, and it was said: on the Heights, and other such opinions. And as for the children of the believers, they are in Paradise according to the majority, and the opposite is that they are in the divine will, and that saying is denied. And this is regarding other than the children of the prophets; as for the children of the prophets, they are in Paradise by consensus. And there is no difference between humans and jinn regarding the blessed and the wretched. The disagreement about jinn is well-known: according to the opinion that they are not obligated before the Master of existence, and according to the opinion of obligation, then the bliss with the Hanafis has three sayings, and the majority including the two companions of Abu Hanifa hold that the obedient among them is blessed in Paradise. And Ibn Hazm narrated the opinion that they are not obligated before our Prophet, peace be upon him, and he said: they were voluntary believers in the law of Moses, peace be upon him. Al-Subki said: 'And there is no doubt that they are obligated in past nations like this nation, either by hearing from the messenger or from a truthful source about him, and that the being human or jinn is not definitive, and the apparent Quran bears witness to al-Dahhak, and the majority are contrary to him.' And it indicates what was mentioned, that Paradise is an abode of eternity for the blessed and the Fire is an abode of eternity for the wretched, the saying of the Most High: 'Then among them are wretched and blessed...' [Hud 11:105] the verse. And the intended meaning of the heavens and the earth in this verse is the ceiling of the Fire and its earth, and the ceiling of Paradise and its earth, not the heaven of the world and its earth, because they will be replaced.
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This passage is a combined definition, classification, and proof. It first defines what is meant by the death of the people of hell: they do not die a true death by soul departure but rather lose sensation of pain, with a minority opinion that they truly die. Then it classifies the wretched (al-shaqi): those who die upon disbelief, including the ignorant disbeliever, the obstinate one, and one who failed in inquiry while neglecting obligatory imitation. Children of polytheists are excluded from the wretched and are in Paradise according to the correct view. Children of believers are in Paradise by majority opinion, with a contrary view that they are under God's will, but the consensus is that children of prophets are in Paradise. The same categories apply to jinn as to humans, with a lengthy note on the disagreement about jinn's obligation. Finally, the author provides a proof from the Quran (Hud 11:105) that Paradise and Hell are eternal abodes, and he interprets 'heavens and earth' in that verse as the ceilings and floors of Hell and Paradise, not the worldly heavens and earth.

Key Terms
سعيد
شقي
خلود
سقف
أرض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the heavens and earth mentioned in the verse are the physical ones we see.
Correction: The commentator clarifies it means the ceilings and floors of Paradise and Hell.

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what do 'heavens and earth' refer to in Hud 11:105?
A) The physical heavens and earth
B) The ceilings and floors of Paradise and Hell
C) The Garden of Eden
D) The sky and ground of the world

Key Takeaway
Surah Hud 11:105 proves that Paradise and Hell are eternal, and 'heavens and earth' refer to their ceilings and floors.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that Paradise and Hell are eternal, how would your daily choices change? What is one decision you are currently putting off that would become urgent if you saw the abode of eternity as your only destination?
?
The verse comes as a warning and a promise. Are you more motivated by the fear of eternal punishment or the hope of eternal reward? Which one actually shapes your actions today, and what does that reveal about your faith?
?
The commentator clarifies that the heavens and earth mentioned are not the ones we see now. This world is temporary. If you are building something in this life—career, relationships, legacy—how much of it will survive into the next? What are you actively investing in that will endure past the replacement of the heavens and earth?

The Punishment and Resurrection of Sinful Believers
The commentator narrates a hadith about sinful believers being punished, then resurrected and brought to paradise.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the process of punishment, death, and eventual resurrection of sinful believers as described in a prophetic hadith and explained by al-Nawawi.

Core Idea
Sinful believers are purified through punishment and then enter paradise.

In this lesson, we explore a prophetic hadith that describes the fate of sinful believers. After being punished for their sins, they are caused to die a true death, become like charcoal, and through intercession are brought to the rivers of paradise where they are revived. Al-Nawawi's commentary clarifies the nature of this death and the stages leading to their entry into paradise.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith carefully
Read the Arabic hadith and its English translation. Notice the sequence: punishment, death, becoming charcoal, intercession, being brought as bundles to the rivers of paradise, and then revived like seeds.
The hadith uses vivid imagery like 'charcoal' and 'bundles'.
2
Understand the role of intercession
After the believers become charcoal, intercession is permitted. This shows that despite their sins, they are not abandoned. Consider the mercy of Allah in allowing intercession for them.
3
Reflect on al-Nawawi's commentary
Al-Nawawi explains that the death is real and removes sensation. The believers are punished in the fire without sensation, then brought out as charcoal and carried to paradise. Reflect on how this clarifies the hadith's meaning.
This commentary helps reconcile the hadith with other teachings about punishment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بخطاياهم، فأماتهم الله إماتة حتى إذا كانوا فحماً أَذِنَ بالشفاعة، فجيء بهم ضبائر ضبائر، فينوا على أنخار الجنة، ثم قيل: يا أهل الجنة؛ أفيضوا عليهم، فينبتون نبات الحبة تكون في حميل السيل. والضبائر: الجماعات. قال النووي في شرحه (۳۸۳): معناه أن المذنبين من المؤمنين يُميتهم الله إماتة بعد أن يُعذبوا المدة التي أرادها الله تعالى، وهذه الإماتة حقيقية يذهب معها الإحساس، ويكون عذابهم على قدر ذنوبهم، ثم يميتهم، ثم يكونون محبوسين في النار من غير إحساس المدة التي قدرها الله تعالى، ثم يخرجون من النار موتى قد صاروا فَحمى، فيُحملون ضبائر ضبائر كما تُحمل الأمتعة ويُلقون على أنهار الجنة.
Because of their sins, God will cause them to die such that when they become charcoal, He will permit intercession, then they will be brought in bundles upon bundles, and they will be thrown upon the rivers of paradise. Then it will be said: O people of paradise, pour upon them. So they will grow like the growth of a seed in a flood carrying torrent. And al-dhaba'ir (الضبائر) means groups. Al-Nawawi said in his commentary (383): Its meaning is that the sinful believers – God will cause them to die after they have been punished for the period God willed, and this death is a true death by which sensation is removed, and their punishment is according to the extent of their sins, then He will cause them to die, then they will be detained in the Fire without sensation for the period God willed, then they will be brought out of the Fire dead having become charcoal, and they will be carried in bundles as loads are carried and thrown upon the rivers of paradise.
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This passage presents a prophetic hadith about the fate of sinful believers, followed by an explanation by al-Nawawi. It describes the process: because of their sins, God causes them to die a true death after punishment, then they become charcoal, then intercession is permitted, and they are brought as bundles and thrown on the rivers of paradise, where they grow like seeds. Al-Nawawi clarifies that this death is real and sensation is removed, and that after their punishment period, they are detained without sensation, then brought out as charcoal and carried like loads to the rivers of paradise.

Key Terms
الضبائر
إماتة
فحم
شفاعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think sinful believers are not punished at all for their sins before entering paradise.
Correction: This hadith shows that sinful believers will be punished and then caused to die a real death before being resurrected and brought to paradise, affirming temporary punishment for their sins.

Checkpoint
According to the hadith, what happens to sinful believers after they become charcoal?
A) They are left in the fire forever
B) They are thrown into the rivers of paradise
C) They are resurrected immediately
D) They are turned into animals

Key Takeaway
Sinful believers experience a real death after punishment, then are brought to paradise and revived.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
After reading this hadith, do you still take your minor sins lightly, knowing they may cause you to undergo a real death and punishment before entering paradise? What will you change today to avoid that state?
?
This hadith shows that even after punishment, believers are revived and enter paradise. How does this knowledge affect your hope in God's mercy? Are you relying on that mercy to delay repentance, or are you actively striving to purify your soul now?
?
If you were to become charcoal in the Fire, would you have any intercessor to help you? What is your relationship with the Prophet and the righteous such that they would plead for you? Commit to one action today to strengthen that connection.

The Eternal Punishment and Bliss and the Rejection of Habituation
The commentator explains the verse 'معذب منعم' and refutes the claim that hell's inhabitants become accustomed to punishment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic doctrine of eternal punishment and bliss in the afterlife, and the refutation of the claim that hell's inhabitants become habituated to punishment.

Core Idea
The bliss of paradise culminates in seeing God; hell's torments never become tolerable.

This passage from the commentary explains two key points about the afterlife: the nature of eternal punishment and bliss, and a refutation of a false idea that hell's inhabitants would get used to the pain. The author grounds the refutation in a direct Quranic verse. As you read, notice how the commentator defines 'معذب منعم' and then counters the erroneous claim.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and English side by side. Notice the structure: definitions first, then refutation.
2
Identify the two groups and their experiences
Find where the commentator describes the torments of hell (zamharir, snakes, scorpions) and the bliss of paradise (highest: vision of God).
3
Analyze the refutation of habituation
Read the sentence starting with 'وما يقال' to understand the false claim and how it is refuted using Quran 78:30.
The Quranic verse is key to the argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوله: (مُعَذَّبٌ مُنَعَمٌ) أي: فداخل النار مُعذَّبٌ فيها بأنواع العذاب: كالزمهرير والحيات والعقارب وغير ذلك. وداخل الجنة مُنعم فيها بأنواع النعيم: وأعلاه رؤية وجه الله الكريم. وقوله: (مَهْمَا بَقِي) أي مدة بقاء كل من الفريقين في إحدى الدارين. وما يُقال: يتمرن أهل النار بالعذاب، حتى لو ألقوا في الجنة لتألموا .. مدسوس على القوم. كيف وقد قال تعالى: ﴿فَذُوقُوا فَلَن تَرِيدَكُمْ إِلَّا عَذَابًا [النبا : ١٣٠]
And his statement: 'tormented, blissful' means: the one in the Fire is tormented therein with types of torment: such as zamharir (extreme cold), snakes, scorpions, and other things. And the one in Paradise is blissful therein with types of bliss: the highest of which is the vision of the noble face of God. And his statement: 'as long as remains' means the duration of the stay of each of the two groups in one of the two abodes. And what is said: that the inhabitants of the Fire become trained to punishment, to the point that if they were thrown into Paradise they would be pained – is a forgery against the people. How could that be, when the Most High said: 'So taste, and We will not increase you except in punishment' [An-Naba 78:30].
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the poem's line about eternal torment and bliss. It first defines 'tormented and blissful': the one in the Fire experiences various torments like extreme cold (zamharir), snakes, scorpions, etc., while the one in Paradise experiences various bliss, the highest being the vision of God. Then it explains that 'as long as remains' means the duration of their stay. Finally, it refutes a false claim that the people of Hell become accustomed to punishment, citing the Quranic verse that they will only increase in punishment.

Key Terms
معذب
منعم
الزمهرير
رؤية وجه الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: People think hell's inhabitants get used to pain and wouldn't feel it.
Correction: The author calls this 'مدسوس على القوم' (a forgery) and cites Quran 78:30 that punishment only increases.

Checkpoint
What is the highest form of bliss in paradise according to this passage?
A) Eating and drinking
B) The vision of God
C) Being with prophets
D) Having no pain

Key Takeaway
The torment of hell is eternal and ever-increasing, while the bliss of paradise culminates in the vision of God; the idea of habituation is a falsehood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever assumed that a sin you repeat becomes 'manageable' or less dangerous? How does the verse 'We will not increase you except in punishment' shatter that illusion for you specifically?
?
If the highest joy in Paradise is seeing God, what does your current daily pursuit of happiness reveal about what you truly value?
?
Could you honestly say that the fear of eternal, ever-increasing punishment has changed one concrete habit in your life this week? If not, what will you do about it before tomorrow?

The Physical Forms of the Blessed and Damned
Description of resurrection bodies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the physical descriptions of believers in paradise and disbelievers in hell based on transmitted sources.

Core Idea
The blessed and damned have distinct physical forms that reflect their states.

This short but significant passage from the matn provides concrete details about the resurrection bodies. The author first notes that people are raised in the state they died, then describes the uniform perfection of believers in paradise and the monstrous size of disbelievers in hell. This lesson unpacks these descriptions and their basis in transmitted knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal English translation. Notice the concise style and the two distinct parts.
2
Identify the two categories described
The passage describes believers in paradise and disbelievers in hell. List the specific attributes given for each group.
Believers: hairless, beardless, 33 years, 60x7 cubits, unchanging. Disbelievers: varying sizes, tooth like Uhud, thigh like Wariqan.
3
Understand the significance as sam'iyyat
Recognize that these details are matters of the unseen (sam'iyyat) which are accepted based on revelation, not reason. They affirm the reality of the afterlife and God's power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فائدة: الناسُ يكونون في الموقف على حالتهم التي ماتوا عليها، ثم يدخل المؤمنون الجنة جُرْداً مُرْداً أبناء ثلاث وثلاثين سنةً، طول كلِّ واحدٍ منهم ستون ذراعاً، وعرضه سبعة أذرع، ثم لا يزيدون ولا ينقصون (1). (2) المصنّف». وأما أجسام الكفار فمختلفة المقادير، حتى ورد أن ضِرْسَ الكافر في النار مثل أُحُدٍ، وفخذه مثل وَرِقَان؛ وهما جبلان بالمدينة، كما في شرح.
A benefit: People will be in the standing ground in the state they died upon. Then the believers will enter paradise hairless, beardless, as thirty-three-year-olds, each one's height sixty cubits, and his width seven cubits, then they will not increase nor decrease. And as for the bodies of the disbelievers, they are of varying sizes, to the extent that it is reported that the molar tooth of the disbeliever in the Fire is like Mount Uhud, and his thigh is like Wariqan – which are two mountains in Medina – as in the commentary.
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage provides eschatological details. It first states that people are resurrected in the state they died. Then it describes the believers in paradise: they are hairless, beardless, thirty-three years old, sixty cubits tall, seven cubits wide, and they do not age or change. Then it describes the disbelievers' bodies in hell: they are of varying sizes, with their teeth as large as Mount Uhud and thighs as large as Mount Wariqan, as reported in hadith.

Key Terms
جرد
مرد
ذراع
ضرس الكافر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think believers age in paradise or that all disbelievers have the same body size.
Correction: The text states believers do not increase nor decrease, so they remain in that prime state. Disbelievers' bodies vary in size, with specific examples of enormous proportions.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the height of the believers in paradise?
A) Sixty cubits
B) Thirty cubits
C) Seven cubits
D) Unknown

Key Takeaway
The physical descriptions of the blessed and damned in the afterlife are part of the unseen knowledge that Muslims accept based on revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have read that believers in paradise will have perfect, unchanging bodies—hairless, beardless, thirty-three, of enormous stature, never aging. Does this description fill you with genuine longing, or does it feel distant and unreal? If it feels unreal, ask yourself: is it because you have not truly internalized the reality of the afterlife? What can you do today to make paradise more real in your heart than the fleeting pleasures of this world? Write down one specific action you will take this week to increase your desire for Jannah.
?
The passage says people are raised on the state they died upon. If your soul were to leave your body right now, would you be comfortable with the state you are in? What sin, what attachment, what heedlessness are you tolerating that you would not want to meet Allah with? Commit right now to leaving that state—repent, make a plan, and tell someone who will hold you accountable.
?
The description of the disbelievers' bodies—enormous, agonizing—is meant to be a warning. Are there people in your life whom you love but who are indifferent to the reality of Hell? How does this passage compel you to speak to them? Write down the name of one person you will share this lesson with this week, and pray for guidance before you do.

The Obligation of Belief in the Prophet's Basin
The commentator explains the poem line about obligatory belief in the Prophet's basin and clarifies the ruling on denial.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that belief in the Prophet's basin is obligatory based on transmitted reports, but denial does not constitute disbelief, only sin, and you will learn the refutation of the Mu'tazila position.

Core Idea
Belief in the Prophet's basin is obligatory; denial is sin, not disbelief.

This lesson addresses a matter of the unseen (samiyyat): the Prophet's basin. The poet declares belief in it obligatory, and the commentator explains the ruling on denial, refuting the Mu'tazila who rejected it.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic poem line and the commentator's explanation. Note the key terms.
2
Identify the ruling on denial
The commentator states that denying the basin does not make one a disbeliever but a sinner. Consider why this distinction matters.
3
Understand the refutation of Mu'tazila
The author refutes the Mu'tazila who denied the basin. Reflect on how transmitted reports (naql) establish this belief.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجوبُ الإيمان بحوض النبي
١١١ - إِيْمَانُنا بِحَوْضِ خَيْرِ الرُّسُلِ حَتْمٌ كَمَا قَدْ جَاءَنَا فِي النَّقْل
قوله: (إِيْمَانُنا بِحَوْضِ خَيْرِ الرُّسُلِ حَتْمٌ) أي: تصديقنا بالحوض الذي يعطاه في الآخرة أفضل المرسلين؛ وهو نبينا محمد ﷺ واجب، لكن لا يكفر من أنكره، وإنما يفسق، وقد نفته المعتزلة، ولذلك أشار المصنف للردّ عليهم بما ذكر.
The obligation of belief in the basin of the Prophet. 111 - Our belief in the basin of the best of messengers is obligatory, as it has come to us in transmission. His statement: 'Our belief in the basin of the best of messengers is obligatory' means: our affirmation of the basin which will be given to the best of messengers in the afterlife – and he is our Prophet Muhammad (ﷺ) – is obligatory. However, whoever denies it does not become a disbeliever, but only becomes a sinner. The Mu'tazila have denied it, and that is why the author indicated a refutation against them by what he mentioned.
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage introduces the topic of the Prophet's basin. It states that belief in the basin is obligatory based on transmitted reports. However, denial of the basin does not lead to disbelief but only to sin (fisq). The Mu'tazila are noted as having denied the basin, and the author refutes them.

Key Terms
حوض النبي
المعتزلة
حتم
فسق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Denying the Prophet's basin is an act of disbelief.
Correction: The commentator clarifies that denial is only a sin (fisq), not disbelief, as long as the person does not reject the transmitted reports entirely.

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what is the ruling on denying the Prophet's basin?
A) It is disbelief
B) It is not disbelief but sin
C) It is permissible
D) It is mandatory to deny

Key Takeaway
Belief in the Prophet's basin is obligatory, but denial is not disbelief; it is a sin, and the Mu'tazila are refuted by transmitted evidence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever dismissed a transmitted matter as unimportant, just because it seemed secondary? How does this lesson's emphasis on the obligation of belief in the basin challenge that attitude? What will you change starting today?
?
If you were to stand before the Prophet's basin, would you be among those who believed and drank, or among those who denied and were turned away? What does your current level of certainty about the basin say about your faith?
?
The Mu'tazila rejected the basin based on their intellect. Are there any aspects of the unseen that you subtly rationalize away? What step will you take tonight to strengthen your submission to transmitted reports?

4 min
Eternal Punishment and Bliss
Commentator explains the eternal punishment and bliss of the two groups and refutes the claim of habituation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nature of eternal punishment and bliss as described by the commentator, and why the claim of habituation in Hell is false.

Core Idea
Eternal bliss includes vision of Allah; eternal punishment never becomes tolerable.

The commentator clarifies two key phrases from the poem: the reality of eternal torment for the damned and eternal delight for the blessed, with the highest delight being the vision of Allah. He then refutes a false notion that Hell's inhabitants become accustomed to suffering.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the literal English translation. Notice the two main parts: explanation of 'punished, blissful' and the refutation of habituation.

List the specific punishments and blisses mentioned. What is the highest bliss? Which Qur'anic verse is cited to refute habituation?
3

The commentator calls the claim of habituation 'an intrusion' and uses Q. 78:30 to prove that punishment only increases. Reflect on the theological significance of this.
